The Dual Definition of Iman and al-Razi's Argument
Sanusi defines iman linguistically and in shari'a, and presents al-Razi's argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dual definition of iman and al-Razi's argument that distinguishes linguistic affirmation from true faith.

Core Idea
Iman in language is affirmation; in shari'a it is restricted to all known necessarily from religion.

This passage begins by distinguishing the linguistic and shari'a meanings of iman, a foundation for theological discussion. It then presents a subtle argument by Imam al-Razi that highlights the difference between mere affirmation and true faith that excludes polytheism. Understanding this distinction is key to later debates on the nature of iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a clarification about tawhid and negative attributes.
2
Identify the two definitions
Find where the author defines iman in language and in shari'a. The linguistic definition is absolute, the shari'a definition is restricted to all things known by necessity from religion.
3
Analyze al-Razi's argument
Al-Razi argues that the verse uses the linguistic meaning of iman (affirmation), which can coexist with polytheism. Therefore, the iman that is incompatible with polytheism must be different from mere affirmation. Follow the objection and answer.
This argument supports the view that iman is not just affirmation but includes action or something else.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سبحانه وتعالى ( والتصديق بالله لا ينافي الشرك إذ لعله بوجوده وصفاته ) الحقيقة هو لا بالتوحيد) الذي هو من الصفات السلبية، وحاصله أن الإيمان في اللغة التصديق مطلقاً وفي الشرع هو التصديق مقيداً بأمر مخصوص هو جميع ما علم كونه من الدين ضرورة والمذكور في الآية محمول على معناه اللغوي، واعلم أن الإمام الرازي قرر في النهاية الوجه الثالث هكذا : المراد بالإيمان هنا التصديق وهو مجامع للشرك فالإيمان الذي لا يجامع الشرك وجب أن يكون مغايراً للتصديق، ثم أجاب عنه بأن ذلك حجة عليكم لأن أفعال الواجبات قد تجامع الشرك والإيمان لا يجامعه فدل على أن فعل الواجبات ليس بالإيمان وعلى هذا التقرير يظهر اشتراك الإلزام لا على ما في الكتاب (احتج الآخرون القائلون بأن الإيمان فعل الطاعات بأسرها، والقائلون بأن الإيمان فعل الطاعات بأسرها والقائلون بأنه مركب من التصديق والإقرار والعمل جميعاً، ) بقوله عليه السلام : ( الإيمان بضع وسبعون شعبة أعلاها قول لا إله إلا قوله : ( لا على ما في الكتاب حيث بدل التقرير وأقام المنافاة مقام المجامعة، فليتأمل.
Glory be to Him and exalted (And affirmation of God does not contradict polytheism, because perhaps it is by His existence and attributes) the reality is it is not by tawhid (which is one of the negative attributes). Its summary is that iman in language is absolute affirmation (tasdiq), and in shari'a it is affirmation restricted to a specific matter: everything known by necessity to be from the religion. And what is mentioned in the verse is carried on its linguistic meaning. Know that Imam al-Razi established in al-Nihaya the third aspect thus: What is meant by iman here is affirmation, and it is compatible with polytheism. So iman that is incompatible with polytheism must be different from affirmation. Then he answered it by saying that that is an argument against you, because acts of obligations may be compatible with polytheism whereas iman is not compatible with it, so it indicates that performing obligations is not iman. And according to this presentation the shared nature of the implication appears, not as in the book. (Others who hold that iman is all acts of obedience, and those who hold that iman is all acts of obedience, and those who hold that it is composed of affirmation, oral confession, and action all together, protested by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Iman has seventy-some branches, the highest of which is the saying 'There is no god but Allah'. His saying: (Not as in the book where he changed the presentation and set up incompatibility in place of compatibility, so ponder.)
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage defines iman in both linguistic and technical senses, then presents an argument by Imam al-Razi. The author first clarifies that iman linguistically is absolute affirmation (tasdiq), while in shari'a it is affirmation restricted to everything known by necessity from the religion. He then notes that the verse in question is interpreted in the linguistic sense. Al-Razi's position is that the 'iman' mentioned in the verse is mere affirmation, which can coexist with polytheism, so the iman that is incompatible with polytheism (i.e., true faith) must be something other than affirmation. Al-Razi then answers an objection: the fact that obligations can coexist with polytheism while iman cannot shows that performing obligations is not iman. The commentary then notes that this presentation differs from that in the book, and the commentator advises pondering the matter.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الشرك
التوحيد
الصفات السلبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That iman always means the same thing in every context.
Correction: Iman has a linguistic meaning (absolute affirmation) and a shari'a meaning (restricted to known articles of faith); the verse uses the linguistic sense.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of iman in shari'a?
A) Absolute affirmation
B) Affirmation restricted to everything known by necessity from the religion
C) All acts of obedience
D) Both affirmation and action

Key Takeaway
Iman in the shari'a is not mere affirmation but a specific belief in everything known necessarily from the religion, which is incompatible with polytheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your faith may include linguistic affirmation, but does it rise to the shari'a definition—firm conviction in everything known necessarily from the religion? Which matters of the religion do you struggle to accept with full certainty, and what are you going to do this week to strengthen that conviction?
?
Al-Razi argues that actions can coexist with polytheism, but true iman cannot. Are any of your good deeds tainted by hidden shirk, such as seeking praise or status? Identify one action you performed recently and examine your intention; commit to purifying it solely for Allah.
?
If true iman is incompatible with polytheism, then where is the line in your heart? Do you have any attachments, fears, or hopes that rival your trust in Allah? Write down one specific distraction that diminishes your tawhid and resolve to remove it starting today.

The Highest Branch of Iman: Interpreting the Hadith
Objection and multiple responses about the highest branch of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars interpret the hadith that 'La ilaha illa Allah' is the highest branch of iman, and why it does not contradict the view that iman is inner affirmation.

Core Idea
The shahada is the foundation, not necessarily superior in every way.

The hadith stating that the highest branch of iman is 'La ilaha illa Allah' appears to elevate the shahada above inner belief. This creates a challenge for those who define iman as inner affirmation. In this lesson, we examine the several subtle responses scholars have given to reconcile the hadith with that definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice the objection and the series of responses.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the objection
The objection states that the hadith, if taken literally, implies the shahada is higher than inner affirmation. Understand why this is problematic.
3
List the four responses
The passage gives four distinct interpretations: specification by consensus, preservation of blood, absolute increase, and foundational role. Write them down.
Each response offers a different angle to defuse the objection.
4
Understand the final point
The last response explains that the shahada is the foundation upon which all other acts depend, giving it a unique precedence.
This is the most comprehensive reply.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this discussion preserves the definition of iman as affirmation while honoring the hadith.
It shows the depth of kalam reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والقائلون بأنه مركب إلخ يرد عليهم أن الحديث على ما حملوه عليه يدل على أن الشهادة أعلى وأفضل من التصديق القلبي بجميع ما علم مجيء الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بالضرورة، وليس كذلك ويمكن أن يدفع بأنه مخصص بالإجماع أو يريد أنها أفضل منه من حيث أنها تحقن الدماء والإذلال لأنها أفضل منه من كل وجه أو المراد بإضافة أفعل التفضيل هاهنا الزيادة المطلقة لا الزيادة على المضاف إليه أي المشهور المعروف من بينها بالفضل بين أهل الملل قوله : لا إله إلا الله، وبهذا أيضاً يندفع ما قيل من أن الحديث يدل على أفضلية قولنا : لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله من الصلاة والحج وأمثالهما مع أن الأمر بالعكس، وأما ما قيل في الجواب أن أفضليته من حيث أنه سبب لعصمة الأنفس والدماء والأموال لا مطلقاً وفيه بحث لأن من الصلاة والحج الشرعيين أيضاً كذلك، وقد يقال : أفضليته من حيث أنه أساس الكل وما لم يوجد لم يعتبر شيئا منها ففيه حيثيتان ليستا في غيره من الأعمال وهو التقدم والتوقف عليه .
His saying: (And those who hold that it is composed, etc.) It is objected against them that the hadith, according to their interpretation, indicates that the testimony (shahada) is higher and better than the inner affirmation of everything known by necessity that the Messenger (peace be upon him) brought, and that is not the case. It can be repelled by saying that it is specified by consensus, or that He intends that it is better than it in that it preserves blood and prevents humiliation, because it is better than it in every respect, or what is meant by the addition of the comparative here is absolute increase, not increase over the object of comparison, i.e., the well-known among them in virtue among the people of religions. His saying: 'There is no god but Allah'. And by this, what is said that the hadith indicates the superiority of our saying 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' over prayer and pilgrimage and the like, while the opposite is the case, is also repelled. As for what is said in answer, that its superiority is that it is the cause of the protection of lives, blood, and wealth, not absolutely, and there is discussion in it because the prayer and pilgrimage according to the Shari'a also do that. And it may be said: Its superiority lies in that it is the foundation of everything, and if it were not present, none of them would be considered, so it has two aspects not present in other acts: precedence and dependence upon it.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection raised by those who claim that iman is composed of affirmation, confession, and action. They use the hadith that the highest branch is 'La ilaha illa Allah' to argue that the shahada is superior to inner affirmation, which would contradict the view that iman is just affirmation. The author presents several responses: First, the hadith may be specified by consensus. Second, the shahada is better only in terms of preserving blood and preventing humiliation. Third, the comparative 'higher' may indicate absolute superiority, not superiority over the object of comparison, i.e., it is simply the most famous virtuous act. Fourth, the shahada's superiority is as the foundation upon which all other acts depend. The author then uses this to also repudiate the claim that the full shahada is superior to prayer and pilgrimage, arguing that prayer and pilgrimage also protect lives, etc., but the shahada has the unique aspect of being the basis.

أفعل التفضيل
الإجماع
التصديق القلبي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith necessarily means the shahada is superior to inner affirmation in every respect.
Correction: The passage shows that the hadith can be interpreted in multiple ways that do not require absolute superiority, such as being specified, limited in scope, or understood as foundational.

Key Takeaway
The apparent superiority of the shahada over inner affirmation is reconciled through nuanced interpretations, especially its role as the foundation of all other acts.

What would it look like to give the shahada its due reverence? Commit to spending 5 minutes today reflecting on its meaning and your sincerity.
?
If someone asked you why you believe the shahada is the most important statement, what would you say? After this lesson, you can give a deeper answer: it is the root without which nothing else stands. Are you building your faith on this solid root? The Meaning of 'Bid'' and the Number of Branches of Faith
The author discusses the meaning of 'bid'' and the number of branches in the hadith, including the theological clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic meaning of 'bid'' in the hadith, the different scholarly views on whether the number indicates a specific count or mere multiplicity, and the theological distinction between the branches of faith and the essence of faith.

Core Idea
The hadith's 'seventy-some' branches emphasizes great multiplicity, not a fixed count.

In this passage, the commentator delves into the famous hadith about the branches of faith. The key word 'bid'' has a specific range in Arabic, and scholars debated whether the number is literal or a hyperbolic expression. Moreover, the passage clarifies a crucial theological point: the branches of faith are not equivalent to the essence of faith itself, so lacking a branch does not negate faith entirely. This lesson unpacks these linguistic and doctrinal layers.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic meaning of 'bid''
Learn that 'bid'' means a number between three and nine, and see how it is used in the hadith. Notice the refutation of al-Jawhari's claim.
The author shows that 'bid'' can be used with tens.
2
Examine the views on the number's significance
Explore the different interpretations: some say the number indicates literal count, others say it indicates multiplicity, and some say it is seventy-seven. The author favors the interpretation of exaggeration using seventy as a base.
Seventy is often used in Arabic for multiplicity.
3
Grasp the theological distinction between branches and essence
Understand why the hadith must refer to branches of faith, not faith itself, by considering the example of removing harm from the road. The Salaf's explanation clarifies that actions are non-essential parts.
This prevents the misunderstanding that missing a branch means loss of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (الإيمان بضع وسبعون أي الإيمان الكامل الذي في أعلى مراتبه وهو المشتمل على أصوله وفروعه الإسلامية وفرضها وواجبها ومندوبها والبضع في العدد بكسر الباء، وبعض العرب يفتحها، وهو ما بين الثلاث إلى التسع وهذا الحديث حجة على الجوهري، حيث زعم أنه يقال : بضع سنين وبضعة عشر رجلاً وبضع عشرة امرأة، فإذا جاوز لفظة العشرة ذهب البضع فلا يقال بضع وعشرون . قيل : المراد بالعدد المذكور مجرد الكثرة لا الحصر لأن خصائل الإيمان أكثر منه، ويدور في خلدي والله أعلم أن المراد المبالغة في الكثرة لأن سبعين يستعمل للكثرة كثيراً قال الله تعالى : في سلسلة ذرعها سبعون ذراعاً [الحاقة: ٣٢]، فلما زاد على ما يستعمل في الكثرة بعد ذكره آل المعنى إلى أنه أكثر من الكثير، وذهب بعض العلماء إلى أن المراد سبع وسبعون وقد جاء في رواية الإيمان سبع وسبعون ونص الراغب الأصفهاني في الله وأدناها إماطة الأذى عن الطريق » . الجواب : إن المراد شعب الإيمان قطعاً لا نفس الإيمان فإن إماطة الأذى عن الطريق ليس داخلاً في أصل الإيمان حتى يكون فاقداً وغير مؤمن بالإجماع فلا بد في الحديث من تقدير مضاف والمصنف لم يورد دليل القائلين بأن الإيمان هو المعرفة أو التصديق مع الإقرار . قوله: (ليس داخلاً في أصل الإيمان إلخ ) قال السلف : كون الأعمال شعبة من الإيمان لا ينافي كونها جزءاً منه ولا يدل على استلزام انتفائها انتفاؤه لجواز أن يكون أجزاء غير أصلية له، نظير هذا أنه لو قرى سورة بتمامها كان كلها فرضاً وإذا ترك بعضها لم يكن تارك فرض .
His saying: (Faith has seventy-some branches), i.e., perfect faith which is at its highest levels, and it includes its Islamic principles and branches, its obligatory, required, and recommended. Al-bid' in number is with kasra of the ba', and some Arabs pronounce it with fatha, and it is between three and nine. This hadith is evidence against al-Jawhari, who claimed that one says 'bida' sanim' and 'bida'ata ashar rajulan' and 'bida'ata ishrata imra'a', but when the word 'ten' is exceeded, the word bid' disappears, so one does not say 'bida' wa ishrun'. It is said: The intended number is merely multiplicity, not enumeration, because the qualities of faith are more than that. And it occurs to my mind, and Allah knows best, that what is intended is exaggeration in multiplicity, because 'seventy' is often used for multiplicity. Allah said: 'In a chain of seventy cubits' [69:32]. So when it increased beyond what is used for multiplicity after mentioning it, the meaning becomes that it is more than many. And some scholars held that what is intended is seventy-seven, and it has come in a narration that faith is seventy-seven. And al-Raghib al-Isfahani stated in ... 'And its lowest is removing harm from the road.' The answer: What is meant is the branches of faith, certainly not faith itself, because removing harm from the road is not included in the essence of faith such that one who lacks it is a disbeliever by consensus. So an implied word must be assumed in the hadith. And the author did not present the proof of those who say that faith is knowledge or affirmation with confession. His saying: (It is not included in the essence of faith, etc.) The Salaf said: That actions are a branch of faith does not contradict them being part of it, nor does it imply that their absence negates faith, because it is possible that they are non-essential parts. An analogy: if one recites a whole surah, all of it is obligatory, but if one leaves some part, he is not considered to have left an obligatory duty.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed linguistic and theological analysis of the hadith about the seventysome branches. It begins by explaining that 'bidth' means a number between three and nine, and that the hadith refers to perfect faith in its highest levels. The author notes that this hadith disproves al-Jawhari's claim about the usage of 'bidth'. He then presents the view that the number is not literal but indicates multiplicity, since seventy is often used for exaggeration. He shares his own opinion that the doubling emphasizes great multiplicity. Some scholars say it is exactly seventy-seven. The hadith is then completed with the lowest branch: removing harm from the road. The response clarifies that the hadith refers to the branches of faith (shu'ab), not faith itself, because removing harm is not part of the essence of faith. Therefore, an implied word must be assumed. Finally, the Salaf's position is given: actions can be branches of faith without being essential parts, similar to reciting a complete surah where all parts are obligatory but leaving some does not make one a deserter of obligation.

Key Terms
بضع
شعب الإيمان
أصل الإيمان
السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith's mention of branches means that each branch is an essential part of faith, so missing one invalidates faith.
Correction: The passage clarifies that actions are branches but not essential parts; lacking a branch does not necessarily negate faith, as seen with removing harm from the road.

Checkpoint

A) Because removing harm is not a religious act
B) Because lacking such an act does not make one a disbeliever by consensus
C) Because the hadith explicitly says so
D) Because the lowest branch is less important

Key Takeaway
The hadith's use of 'bid'' and 'seventy' emphasizes the great multiplicity of faith's branches, but these branches are not the essence of faith itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lowest branch is removing harm from the road. When was the last time you deliberately ignored a small act of kindness because you felt it was beneath you? Does your attitude toward 'small' deeds reflect a heart that truly values the branches of faith, or a sense of entitlement?
?
The author suggests the number in the hadith is an exaggeration for multiplicity. Are you comfortable with ambiguity in matters of religion, or do you insist on precise definitions? Could your demand for certainty be a way to avoid the effort of acting on the many branches?
?
The Salaf held that actions are not essential parts of faith, so lacking a branch does not negate iman. Does this truth make you more grateful, or does it tempt you to be lazy about acts of worship? Honestly, which tendency is stronger in your life right now, and what will you do about it today?

Iman's Increase and Decrease: A Verbal Dispute
Al-Razi argues the dispute is verbal and shows the conclusion based on the definition of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi considers the dispute over iman's increase and decrease to be a verbal disagreement dependent on the definition of iman.

Core Idea
Al-Razi shows the dispute is verbal: it hinges on how you define iman.

This lesson examines al-Razi's argument that the dispute over whether iman can increase or decrease is not a substantive theological disagreement but a verbal one. The key is the definition of iman: if it is affirmation (tasdiq), it cannot vary; if it is actions, it clearly can. Understanding this clarifies a major point in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Razi's Claim
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note that al-Razi states the dispute is verbal because it depends on the interpretation of iman.
Look for the phrase 'هو بحث لفظي'.
2
Examine the First Definition
Understand why, if iman is defined as affirmation (tasdiq), it cannot increase or decrease. Notice the reasoning: certainty (yaqin) does not admit variation, and its object is a fixed whole.
3
Examine the Second Definition
Understand why, if iman is defined as actions (alone or with affirmation), it clearly accepts increase and decrease.
Al-Razi calls this 'ظاهر' (obvious).
4
Reflect on the Implications
Consider why this matters: many theological disputes are actually verbal, and clarifying definitions can resolve them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثاني : في إثبات أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص ] ذاته ) في أن الإيمان هل يزيد وينقص أثبته طائفة ونفاه آخرون قال الإمام الرازي: وكثير من المتكلمين هو بحث لفظي لأنه ( فرع تفسير الإيمان فإن قلنا: هو التصديق فلا يقبلهما لأن الواجب هو اليقين وإنه لا يقبل التفاوت )، لا بحسب ) لأن التفاوت إنما هو لاحتمال النقيض وهو) أي احتماله ( ولو بأبعد وجه ينافي اليقين) فلا يجامعه ولا بحسب متعلقه لأنه جميع ما علم بالضرورة مجيء الرسول به والجميع من حيث هو جميع لا يتصور فيه تعدد وإلا لم يكن جمعاً، وإن قلنا : هو الأعمال إما وحدها أو مع التصديق ( فيقيلهما وهو ظاهر
The second goal: On proving that iman increases and decreases. [Its essence] Concerning whether iman increases and decreases, a group affirmed it and others denied it. Imam al-Razi said: And many of the mutakallimun say it is a verbal dispute because it is a branch of interpreting iman. For if we say it is affirmation (tasdiq), then it does not accept either [increase or decrease] because what is obligatory is certainty, and it does not admit variation, neither in itself, because variation is only due to probability of contradiction, and it (i.e., its probability) even in the most remote sense contradicts certainty, so it is incompatible with it; nor according to its object, because it is everything known by necessity that the Messenger brought, and the whole as a whole is not conceivable to have multiplicity, otherwise it would not be a whole. And if we say it is actions, either alone or with affirmation, then it accepts both, and that is obvious.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage introduces the second major topic: whether iman can increase and decrease. It presents al-Razi's view that the dispute is largely verbal because it depends on the definition of iman. If iman is defined as affirmation (tasdiq), then it cannot increase or decrease because certainty (yaqin) does not admit variation; variation implies the possibility of doubt, which contradicts certainty. Also, the object of affirmation is everything known from the Prophet, which is a fixed set, so multiplicity is not possible. However, if iman is defined as actions (either alone or combined with affirmation), then it clearly can increase and decrease, as actions are variable.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
اليقين
الزيادة والنقصان
بحث لفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The disagreement over iman's increase and decrease is a genuine theological dispute that cannot be resolved.
Correction: Al-Razi argues it is a verbal dispute that arises from different definitions of iman, not a substantive theological disagreement.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, under which definition of iman does it become a verbal dispute whether iman increases and decreases?
A) Only when iman is defined as actions
B) Only when iman is defined as affirmation
C) It is always a verbal dispute regardless of definition
D) It is a verbal dispute because it depends on the interpretation of iman

Key Takeaway
The dispute over iman's increase and decrease is resolved by clarifying the definition of iman: if it is affirmation, no change; if actions, change is possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own iman, do you measure it by your certainty in the truth of the Prophet's message or by your actions? According to al-Razi, if iman is certainty, it cannot change. Does that comfort you or trouble you? Why?
?
If certainty admits no degrees, what does that mean for your moments of doubt? Are you willing to say that any doubt at all—even a fleeting thought—means you lack the yaqin that al-Razi describes as obligatory? Examine your heart honestly: do you truly have certainty, or have you convinced yourself that some doubt is acceptable?
?
Al-Razi reduces the dispute to a matter of definition. But this lesson forces you to decide: What do you actually believe iman is? Your answer determines whether your faith can grow or waver. If it can waver, what does that imply about your salvation? Do you have the courage to settle this question for yourself today, not just intellectually but in your heart?

Affirmation Increases in Strength and Weakness
The author affirms tasdiq's variability in strength and defends against doubt-based objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how affirmation (tasdiq) can increase and decrease in strength and weakness, and how the author defends this view against the objection that variation implies doubt.

Core Idea
Affirmation is a psychological quality that naturally varies in strength without requiring doubt.

In this passage, the author affirms that inward faith (tasdiq) is not static but can increase and decrease. He addresses a key objection: if faith requires certainty, how can it vary? His answer distinguishes variation through doubt from variation through strength and weakness, establishing that qualitative variation is possible even in certain belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation. Notice the author's declaration that tasdiq accepts increase and decrease in two aspects.
2
Identify the first aspect
The first aspect is strength and weakness. The author describes tasdiq as a psychological quality (kayfiyya nafsaniyya) that differs in intensity.
3
Analyze the objection and response
The objection says variation must come from probability of contradiction (i.e., doubt). The author responds that variation can be in strength without any probability of contradiction.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters for theology: faith can be stronger or weaker without being less genuine.
This supports the idea that actions and spiritual practices can increase faith.

And the truth is that affirmation (tasdiq) accepts increase and decrease in two aspects: (i.e., according to essence and according to object. The first: strength and weakness, for affirmation is among the psychological qualities that vary in strength and weakness. (Your statement: The obligatory is certainty, and variation is only through probability of contradiction. We say: We do not concede that variation is only due to that probability, for it is possible that it be by strength and weakness without probability of contradiction. Then (the dharia that the total branches are seventy-two, and he derived that in a subtle way; whoever wishes to see it, let him refer to it. His saying: (It is not included in the essence of faith, etc.) The Salaf said: That actions are a branch of faith does not contradict them being part of it, nor does it imply that their negation negates faith, because it is possible that they are non-essential parts. An analogy: if one recites a whole surah, all of it is obligatory, but if he leaves some part, he is not considered to have left an obligatory duty. His saying: (And if we say it is actions, it accepts both, and that is obvious. If what is meant is absolute acts of obedience, obligatory or supererogatory, leaving or doing, as some hold, then its increase and decrease according to the measure of perseverance or abandonment is obvious. And if what is meant is the obligatory among them, as others hold, then its increase is according to the increase of its times, and its decrease according to the decrease of them or because they become non-obligatory, as in hajj and zakat for the poor. His saying: (The first: strength and weakness. It is said: This is granted but it is of no benefit, because the dispute is only about variation in faith in terms of quantity, i.e., few and many, for increase is most often used for numbers. As for variation in quality, i.e., strength and weakness, it is outside the subject of dispute.

Commentary
This passage asserts that affirmation (tasdiq) does indeed admit increase and decrease, refuting the earlier objection. It gives two aspects: essence (strength/weakness) and object. The first aspect is explained: affirmation is a psychological quality that can vary in strength and weakness. The objection that variation implies probability of contradiction is rejected; variation can be in strength without doubt. The passage then digresses to mention that the total branches are seventy-two according to one scholar. It returns to the Salaf's view that actions can be branches without being essential parts, using the surah analogy. The passage then discusses the implications if iman is defined as actions: if absolute obedience, increase is by perseverance; if only obligatory, increase is by increased times or obligation. Finally, a critique is raised: the dispute is about quantitative (numerical) increase, not qualitative (strength/weakness), so the argument about strength is irrelevant. This shows the debate's nuance.

Correction: The author shows that variation can be in strength and weakness alone, without any probability of contradiction, so faith can be more or less intense while remaining fully certain.

Quantitative vs Qualitative Variation in Faith
The author presents and responds to the quantitative vs qualitative distinction and discusses actions as aspects of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether faith's increase is quantitative (numerical) or qualitative (strength), and how actions relate to faith's increase and decrease.

Core Idea
Faith can increase in quantity through actions but also in quality through strength, though some restrict the debate to quantity.

After establishing that tasdiq can vary in strength, the author turns to a critique: the real dispute is about quantitative increase—like having more or fewer parts of faith. He then discusses how actions (a'mal) relate to faith's increase, showing that whether actions are obligatory or supererogatory affects how faith increases. This lesson clarifies the two types of variation and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation for this lesson. Focus on the distinction between quantity and quality.
2
Understand the critique
The objection states that the dispute is about quantity (kammiyya), i.e., number, and that quality (kayfiyya) is irrelevant. Note the argument that 'increase' is usually used for numbers.
3
Examine the actions discussion
The author presents two interpretations of faith as actions: absolute obedience (including supererogatory) leads to increase by perseverance; only obligatory acts lead to increase by time or obligation status.
4
Synthesize the two types
Recognize that faith can increase both in quantity (by adding acts) and in quality (by intensity), but the passage raises a legitimate debate about which is the primary meaning.

Interpreting the Hadith on Branches of Faith
Answers objection about branches of faith hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the hadith mentioning branches of faith (shuʿab al-īmān) refers to acts and attributes of faith, not to faith itself, and that these acts are non-essential parts whose absence does not negate faith.

Core Idea
Branches of faith are not the root—removing harm from the road does not remove belief.

In this passage, the author addresses a common misinterpretation of a well-known hadith. The hadith lists acts like removing harm from the road as part of faith, leading some to think that failing to perform such acts means one loses faith entirely. The author clarifies that the hadith speaks of branches, not the essence of faith. Let's see how the Salaf explained this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Notice the hadith mentions 'removing harm from the road' as a branch of faith. This might suggest that such acts are essential to faith itself.
The objection arises from taking the hadith literally without considering the intended meaning.
2
Read the author's answer
The author states that the hadith refers to branches of faith, not faith itself. Therefore, an implicit word (taqdīr muḍāf) is necessary.
This is a common interpretive technique in Islamic scholarship.
3
Understand the Salaf's explanation
The Salaf explain that deeds are parts of faith but non-essential parts. Their absence does not negate faith, just as missing part of a surah does not mean one left the entire obligation.
This analogy clarifies the relationship between deeds and faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث - المقصد الثاني : في إثبات أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص الله وأدناها إماطة الأذى عن الطريق. الجواب : إن المراد شعب الإيمان قطعاً لا نفس الإيمان فإن إماطة الأذى عن الطريق ليس داخلاً في أصل الإيمان حتى يكون فاقداً وغير مؤمن بالإجماع فلا بد في الحديث من تقدير مضاف والمصنف لم يورد دليل القائلين بأن الإيمان هو المعرفة أو التصديق مع الإقرار. قوله: (ليس داخلاً في أصل الإيمان إلخ ) قال السلف : كون الأعمال شعبة من الإيمان لا ينافي كونها جزءاً منه ولا يدل على استلزام انتفائها انتفاءه لجواز أن يكون أجزاء غير أصلية له، نظير هذا أنه لو قرى سورة بتمامها كان كلها فرضاً وإذا ترك بعضها لم يكن تارك فرض .
The third observation - the second purpose: on proving that faith increases and decreases. “God, and its lowest is removing harm from the road.” The answer: what is meant is the branches of faith, definitely not faith itself, for removing harm from the road is not included in the essence of faith such that one who lacks it is lacking faith and is not a believer by consensus. So in the hadith there must be an implicit addition. And the author did not cite the proof of those who say that faith is knowledge or assent with confession. His statement: “not included in the essence of faith, etc.” The Salaf said: that deeds are a branch of faith does not preclude them being part of it, nor does it imply that their absence necessitates its absence, because they may be non-essential parts. An analogy for this is that if one recites a complete surah, all of it is obligatory, and if one leaves some of it, one is not leaving an obligation.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage provides an answer to an objection derived from a hadith that mentions the highest and lowest branches of faith, including removing harm from the road. The author clarifies that the hadith refers to the branches (shuʿab) of faith, not to the essence (nafs) of faith. Removing harm from the road is not part of the foundational essence of faith, since by consensus one who does not do it is not considered a non-believer. Therefore, an implicit addition (taqdīr muḍāf) must be assumed in the hadith. The marginal comment (qawluhu) then elaborates: the Salaf held that deeds being a branch (shuʿba) of faith does not preclude them from being a part (juzʾ) of it, but it does not imply that their absence entails the absence of faith entirely, as they are non-essential parts. An analogy is given: reciting a complete surah—all of it is obligatory, but leaving some of it does not mean one has left the entire obligation.

Key Terms
شعب الإيمان
أصل الإيمان
تقدير مضاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a person does not perform acts like removing harm from the road, they lose their faith entirely.
Correction: The hadith calls such acts branches (shuʿab) of faith, not the essence (nafs al-īmān). The Salaf explained they are non-essential parts, so omitting them does not remove faith.

Checkpoint

A) The essence of faith
B) A branch of faith
C) An act that nullifies faith
D) The highest degree of faith

Key Takeaway
The hadith about branches of faith does not make external acts essential to faith; they are non-essential parts that do not negate belief if missed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that even the lowest branch of faith, like removing harm from the road, is a deed that does not define your entire faith. But when you neglect such a deed, do you feel a sense of loss in your connection with Allah? Why does your neglect not shake your confidence in your belief, yet you still feel less righteous? What does that tell you about the state of your heart?
?
The Salaf said that missing a branch does not mean you have left faith entirely. Consider the last time you omitted a good deed you knew was encouraged. Did you secretly excuse yourself by thinking 'it's not essential anyway'? Or did you feel guilty and resolve to do better? Which response aligns with the lesson's teaching, and which reveals neglect? Ask Allah to make you among those who take every branch seriously, not as a condition of faith but as a fruit of it.
?
The analogy of the surah: if you recite most of it but leave one verse, you haven't abandoned the entire surah. In your daily life, are you content with just 'most of the surah'—the big acts of worship—while neglecting the small branches like removing harm (e.g., being kind in your speech, picking up trash)? What is one small branch you will commit to starting today, not to save your faith, but to prove its reality?

The Verbal Debate on Increase of Faith
Al-Razi frames the increase-of-faith debate as verbal, depending on definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the debate on the increase of faith is a verbal dispute that hinges on the definition of faith.

Core Idea
Whether faith increases depends entirely on what we mean by 'faith.'

This passage from al-Razi addresses a classic theological debate: does faith increase or decrease? Al-Razi argues that the dispute is largely verbal, depending on whether faith is defined as inner assent (taṣdīq) or as works (aʿmāl). We will see how each definition leads to a different conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Razi uses a very structured argument.
2
Identify the two definitions of faith
The passage presents two definitions: faith as assent and faith as works. Observe how each definition leads to a different conclusion regarding increase and decrease.
3
Examine the reasoning for assent
For the definition as assent, find the arguments against increase: certainty does not admit variation in essence or object.
The object is the entire revealed message as a whole.
4
Examine the reasoning for works
For works, note the two sub-interpretations: absolute obedience vs. obligatory acts. Understand how increase works for each.
For obligatory acts, increase is by times of obligation.
5
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author asserts that assent does accept increase in two respects. Consider how this modifies the earlier argument.
This shows the issue is not merely definitional but also involves deeper analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في أن الإيمان هل يزيد وينقص أثبته طائفة ونفاه آخرون قال الإمام الرازي: وكثير من المتكلمين هو بحث لفظي لأنه فرع تفسير الإيمان فإن قلنا: هو التصديق فلا يقبلهما لأن الواجب هو اليقين وإنه لا يقبل التفاوت، لا بحسب الذات لأن التفاوت إنما هو لاحتمال النقيض وهو ولو بأبعد وجه ينافي اليقين فلا يجامعه ولا بحسب متعلقه لأنه جميع ما علم بالضرورة مجيء الرسول به والجميع من حيث هو جميع لا يتصور فيه تعدد وإلا لم يكن جمعاً، وإن قلنا: هو الأعمال إما وحدها أو مع التصديق فيقبلهما وهو ظاهر، أما إذا أريد به مطلق الطاعات فرضاً كان أو نفلاً تركاً أو فعلاً كما ذهب إليه البعض فازدياده وانتقاصه بحسب المواظبة عليها وتركها ظاهر، وأما إذا أريد بها ما هو المفروض منها كما ذهب إليه آخرون فازدياده إنما هو بحسب ازدياد أوقاتها وانتقاصه بحسب انتقاصها أو بعدم وجوبها كما في الحج والزكاة للفقير، والحق أن التصديق يقبل الزيادة والنقصان لوجهين: أي بحسب الذات وبحسب المتعلق.
Concerning whether faith increases and decreases, a group affirmed it and others denied it. Imam al-Razi said: and many of the theologians (mutakallimūn) consider it a verbal inquiry because it depends on the interpretation of faith. If we say: it is assent (taṣdīq), then it does not accept either increase or decrease, because what is obligatory is certainty (yaqīn) and it does not admit variation—not with respect to essence (dhāt), because variation is only due to the possibility of the opposite, and even if remote, it contradicts certainty and cannot coexist with it; nor with respect to its object (mutaʿallaq), because it is everything known by necessity that the Messenger brought, and the whole as a whole cannot be conceived as multiple, otherwise it would not be a whole. And if we say: it is works, either alone or with assent, then it accepts them both, and that is apparent. For if what is meant by works is absolute acts of obedience, obligatory or supererogatory, abandonment or performance, as some hold, then its increase and decrease according to perseverance and abandonment is apparent. And if what is meant is the obligatory ones, as others hold, then its increase is according to the increase of their times, and its decrease according to their decrease or the lack of their obligation, as in Hajj and Zakat for the poor. And the truth is that assent (taṣdīq) does accept increase and decrease in two respects: with respect to essence (dhāt) and with respect to object (mutaʿallaq).
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents the debate on whether faith increases and decreases. It begins by noting that some affirm it and others deny it. Al-Razi and many theologians consider it a verbal dispute that depends on how ‘faith’ is defined. If faith is defined as assent (taṣdīq), then it cannot increase or decrease because the required degree is certainty (yaqīn), which admits no variation—neither in its own essence (since variation would require possibility of the opposite, which contradicts certainty) nor in its object (since the object is the entire revealed message as a whole, which cannot be multiple). If faith is defined as works (aʿmāl), whether alone or combined with assent, then it does admit increase and decrease. The passage elaborates on two interpretations of works: if works mean all acts of obedience, increase and decrease are by frequency; if works mean only obligatory acts, increase and decrease depend on times of obligation or exemption. Finally, the author asserts the truth (al-ḥaqq) that assent itself does accept increase and decrease in two respects: with respect to its essence (al-dhāt) and with respect to its object (al-mutaʿallaq).

Key Terms
بحث لفظي
التصديق
اليقين
الأعمال
الذات
المتعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the debate is purely theological and unrelated to definition.
Correction: Al-Razi shows it hinges on the definition of faith; it is a verbal dispute.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, why would faith defined as assent (taṣdīq) not admit increase or decrease?
A) Because assent is by nature infinite
B) Because the required degree is certainty, which has no variation
C) Because works are excluded
D) Because assent is a single act

Key Takeaway
The increase of faith debate is resolved by clarifying what faith means; it is a verbal dispute that depends on definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own faith, do you see it as a static certainty or something that fluctuates? Al-Razi argues that assent itself can increase with respect to essence and object. Have you experienced your faith deepening over time, not just through actions but in the strength of your conviction? What caused that change, and are you actively seeking growth?
?
If faith is defined as works, then your daily actions directly affect your faith. Look at your last week: did your actions increase or decrease your faith? Al-Razi shows that even obligatory acts can vary. For the acts you omitted, do you feel a genuine loss in faith, or do you separate belief from action? How can you reconcile that with this lesson?
?
Al-Razi says the debate is 'verbal' but not trivial. It forces you to define what faith means to you. Is your faith primarily intellectual assent, practical obedience, or both? If you were to judge yourself by the definition that faith is certainty without variation, would you be confident? This lesson demands you move from abstract debate to personal accountability. What is one concrete step you can take today to increase your faith in either essence or object?

Defining Disbelief and the Role of Apparent Acts
Sanusi defines kufr and answers an objection about external signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of disbelief (kufr) as the failure to believe the Messenger in matters known by necessity, and how outward acts can serve as signs of disbelief.

Core Idea
Disbelief is not just denial but any failure to believe the Messenger, including doubt.

This passage from al-Mawaqif tackles a foundational issue in Islamic theology: what exactly constitutes disbelief? The author defines it clearly and then addresses a practical objection about external signs of disbelief. Understanding this helps distinguish between internal belief and external actions, and clarifies that doubt is also a form of disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice the structure: definition, objection, answer, and a clarifying remark.
2
Identify the definition of kufr
Find where the author defines kufr. Note that it is described as the opposite of faith and specifically as 'lack of belief' in the Messenger, not necessarily explicit denial.
The definition includes doubt (shakk) as a form of lack of belief.
3
Understand the objection and the answer
The objection claims that a person who performs outward acts of disbelief (like tying a belt) but believes inwardly is not a disbeliever. The author answers by saying such acts are taken as signs of denial, so the person is judged accordingly.
This shows the importance of external indicators in Islamic jurisprudence.
4
Reflect on the scope of disbelief
Consider that disbelief includes not only explicit denial but also doubt. Why might this be important for theology?
This point is clarified in the marginal note about al-Qadi's definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثالث: في الكفر في الكفر وهو خلاف الإيمان فهو عندنا عدم تصديق الرسول في بعض ما علم مجيئه ضرورة فإن قيل فشاد الزنار ولابس الغيار بالاختيار لا يكون كافراً إذا كان مصدقاً له في الكل وهو باطل إجماعاً، قلنا: جعلنا الشيء الصادر عنه باختياره علامة للتكذيب فحكمنا عليه بذلك، أي بكونه كافراً غير مصدق ولو علم أنه. قوله: (وهو عدم تصديق الرسول عليه السلام سواء كان مكذباً له عليه السلام أو شاكاً في صدقه، وأما ما ذكره في تفسير القاضي من أن الكفر إنكار ما علم بالضرورة مجيء الرسول عليه السلام به فلعل مراده بالإنكار عدم التصديق ليعم الشك.
The third purpose: on disbelief (al-kufr). Disbelief is the opposite of faith. It is, in our view, the failure to believe the Messenger in something that is known by necessity that he brought. For if it is said: one who ties the zunnār (a belt) and wears the ghiyār (distinctive garment) by choice is not a disbeliever if he believes in everything—and that is false by consensus. We say: we made the thing that proceeds from him by choice a sign of denial, so we judge him accordingly, i.e., that he is a disbeliever, not a believer, even if we know that… His statement: (And it is the failure to believe the Messenger, peace be upon him, whether he is denying him or doubting his truthfulness. As for what was mentioned in the commentary of al-Qāḍī, that disbelief is the denial of what is known by necessity that the Messenger brought, perhaps his intention by ‘denial’ is failure to believe, to include doubt.)
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage defines disbelief (al-kufr) as the opposite of faith. According to the author (ʿindanā), disbelief is the failure to believe the Messenger (ʿadam taṣdīq al-rasūl) in anything that is known by necessity that he brought. The passage then addresses an objection: if someone outwardly performs acts associated with disbelief (like tying the zunnār or wearing the ghiyār) but internally believes everything, does that make them a disbeliever? The objection says no, but the author responds that such outward acts are taken as signs (ʿalāma) of denial (takdhīb), and thus the person is judged a disbeliever. The marginal comment (qawluhu) clarifies that disbelief is simply failure to believe the Messenger, whether through explicit denial (takdhīb) or doubt (shakk). It also notes that al-Qāḍī’s definition of disbelief as denial (inkār) of what is known by necessity should be interpreted as ‘failure to believe’ to include doubt.

Key Terms

عدم التصديق
العلامة
التكذيب
الشك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that disbelief only occurs when someone explicitly denies the truth. Doubt or uncertainty about the Messenger's truthfulness is not considered disbelief.
Correction: This passage clearly states that disbelief includes doubt (shakk) about the Messenger's truthfulness. The definition 'failure to believe' covers both denial and doubt.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how is disbelief (kufr) defined?
A) Denial of God's existence
B) Failure to believe the Messenger in something known by necessity
C) Doing any sinful action
D) Wearing distinctive garments of non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
Disbelief is fundamentally the failure to believe the Messenger, and external acts can be evidence for this state; even doubt constitutes disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted any teaching of the Messenger, even a minor one? According to this lesson, doubt is disbelief. Confront that doubt now: what is it, and will you repent and affirm with certainty?
?
Look at your outward actions: is there anything you do that could be a 'sign of denial' to others, like carelessness with Islamic practices or imitating non-Muslims? If so, what change will you make starting today?
?
This lesson says that failure to believe in even one thing the Messenger brought is kufr. Have you taken any command lightly? What is one command you have been neglecting? Commit now to fulfill it properly.

Kufr as the Opposite of Iman
Al-Jurjani defines kufr by contrasting it with iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that kufr is defined relative to one's definition of iman, and that actions alone do not determine kufr without underlying belief.

Core Idea
Kufr is the opposite of iman, and its definition depends on how iman is defined.

Al-Jurjani begins by clarifying that external acts, like tying a sash or prostrating to the sun, are not judged as kufr between the person and God unless they reflect inner belief. He then establishes the foundational principle: kufr is defined as the opposite of iman, so each sect defines kufr according to its own definition of iman. This sets the stage for the sectarian debates to follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the scenario about tying the sash
Notice how Al-Jurjani uses a concrete example to show that external acts alone do not constitute kufr. The act must be accompanied by belief in its truth to be considered kufr.
This scenario illustrates the principle that kufr is a matter of the heart, not just outward action.
2
Consider the case of children of believers
Understand the reasoning that children of believers are considered believers by legal ruling, even without explicit affirmation, because of the parent's faith.
This shows the legal dimension of iman and kufr.
3
Grasp the principle of opposite definitions
Learn that any definition of kufr is simply the negation of what one defines as iman. For those who define iman as knowledge of God, kufr is ignorance; for those who define iman as obedience, kufr is disobedience.
This principle is key to understanding why sects differ on who is a kafir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث - المقصد الثالث : في الكفر
شد الزنار لا لتعظيم دين النصارى واعتقاد حقيته لم يحكم بكفره فيما بينه وبين الله، كما مر في سجود الشمس لا يقال : أطفال المؤمنين لا تصديق لهم، فيلزم أن يكونوا كفاراً لا مؤمنين وهو باطل لأنا نقول : هم مصدقون حكماً لما علم من ضرورة أنه الله كان يجعل إيمان أحد الأبوين إيماناً للأولاد، (وهو) أي الكفر (عند كل طائفة مقابل ما فسره به) الإيمان كما هو عندنا مقابل لما فسرناه به فمن قال : الإيمان معرفة الله قال الكفر هو الجهل بالله وبطلانه ظاهر ومن قال : الإيمان هو الطاعات كالخوارج وبعض المعتزلة قال : الكفر هو المعصية لكنهم اختلفوا ( فقالت الخوارج : كل معصية كفر، وقد أبطلناه وقالت المعتزلة المعاصي ) أقسام ( ثلاثة إذ منها ما يدل على الجهل بالله ووحدته وما يجوز عليه وما لا يجوز، و) الجهل ( برسالة رسوله كإلقاء المصحف في القاذورات واللفظ بكلمات دالة على ذلك) وكسب الرسول والاستخفاف به ) فهو كفر ومنها ما لا يدل على ذلك وهو قسمان : قسم يخرج) مرتكبه ( إلى منزلة بين المنزلتين أي الكفر والإيمان على معنى أنه ( لا يحكم على صاحبها بالكفر (لسائر ما اتصف به من ( أعماله ) الصالحة، (ولا
قوله : ( لأنا) نقول : هم مصدقون حكماً إلخ) وبهذا أيضاً يندفع ما يتوهم من أنه يلزم أن لا يكون النائم مؤمناً، إذ لا تصديق له لأن النوم مضاد للعلم عندنا ووجه الاندفاع أن الشارع جعل التصديق المحقق في حكم الباقي ما لم يطرأ عليه ما يضاده فهو مصدق حكماً، وقد يجاب بأن التصديق ليس بإدراك بل هو كلام نفسي على ما وقع في كلام ،بعضهم ولا نسلم المنافاة بينه وبين النوم ولا يخفى ما فيه .
قوله : (وهو)
كل طائفة يقابل ما فسر به الإيمان رده في شرح المقاصد بأنه لا يستقيم على القول بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين أصلاً، ويمكن دفعه بأن التقابل لا يلزم أن يكون بالإيجاب
والسلب حتى يرد ما ذكره فتأمل.

قوله : ( فقالت :الخوارج كل معصية (كفر فإن قلت : يلزم السلف وأصحاب الأثر القائلين بأن الإيمان تصديق بالجنان وإقرار باللسان وعمل بالأركان أن يقولوا بما قال به الخوارج : بناء على أن الشيء ينتفي بانتفاء ركنه ، ولا منزلة عندهم بين الكفر والإيمان مع أنهم لا يجعلون تارك العمل خارجا من الإيمان ويقطعون بعدم خلوده في النار قلت : أجيب عنه بأن الإيمان يطلق على ما هو الأساس والأصل في دخول الجنة وهو التصديق وحده على ما هو الكامل المنجي، وهو الذي عد العمل ركناً منه وموضع الخلاف أن مطلق الاسم للأول أو الثاني، وقد أشرنا فيما سبق إلى وجه دفع آخر، فليتذكر.
بالإيمان لإيهامه عدم التصديق بل يحكم عليه بالفسق ( ويعبر عنهما ) أي عن المعاصي المخرجة إلى تلك المنزلة بالكبائر) كالقتل العمد والعدوان والزنا وشرب الخمر ونظائرهما وأول من أحدث القول بهذا الإخراج واصل بن عطاء وعمرو بن عبيد، ( ومنها ما لا يخرج أي قسم لا يخرج ) ككشف العورة والسفه، ويسمى بالصغائر ولا يوصف صاحبها بالكفر ولا بالفسق بل بالإيمان ) وسنزيده أي نزيد ما ذكرناه في هذا المقصد من قول الخوارج والمعتزلة بياناً في المقصد الذي يتلوه.
The third observation - the third purpose: on disbelief. Tying the sash not for veneration of the Christian religion and belief in its truth is not judged as his disbelief between him and God, as passed in prostration to the sun. It is not said: The children of believers have no affirmation, so it follows that they would be disbelievers not believers, and that is false; for we say: They are affirmers by legal ruling because it is known from necessity that God used to make the faith of one of the parents a faith for the children. (It) i.e. disbelief (according to each sect is opposite to what it explained faith with) just as with us it is opposite to what we explained it with. Whoever said: faith is knowledge of God, said disbelief is ignorance of God, and its falsehood is apparent. Whoever said: faith is acts of obedience, like the Khawarij and some Mu'tazila, said: disbelief is disobedience, but they differed. (The Khawarij said: every disobedience is disbelief, and we have refuted it. And the Mu'tazila said: acts of disobedience are) three divisions, since from them is what indicates ignorance of God and His oneness and what is possible for Him and what is not, and ignorance of His messenger's message like throwing the Quran into filth and uttering words indicating that, and reviling the messenger and disrespecting him, so it is disbelief. And from them is what does not indicate that, and it is two divisions: a division that takes its perpetrator to a station between the two stations i.e. between disbelief and faith, in the sense that he is not judged with disbelief because of the rest of his righteous deeds, and he is not judged with faith because it suggests lack of affirmation. Rather he is judged with transgression (fisq), and they are expressed as (major sins) like intentional murder and aggression and adultery and drinking wine and their likes. The first to originate the saying of this removal was Wasil ibn 'Ata' and 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. And from them is what does not remove i.e. a division that does not remove, like uncovering the private parts and foolishness, and it is called minor sins, and its possessor is not described with disbelief nor with transgression but with faith. And we will add i.e. increase what we mentioned in this purpose from the saying of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, clarification in the purpose that follows it.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification passage within the larger topic of disbelief (kufr). The author begins by presenting a scenario: tying the sash (a Christian practice) not for veneration or belief in its truth is not judged as disbelief between the person and God, referencing an earlier ruling on prostration to the sun. He then warns that children of believers cannot be denied faith, as they are considered affirmers legally because God made the faith of one parent count for the children. The main definition of kufr is given: each sect defines kufr as the opposite of what they define iman. For example, if iman is knowledge of God, kufr is ignorance of God. If iman is acts of obedience (as the Khawarij and some Mu'tazila hold), then kufr is disobedience (ma'siya). The author then explains the Mu'tazila division of sins into three categories: (1) sins that indicate ignorance of God and His messenger, which are kufr; (2) sins that do not indicate that, which are subdivided into (a) major sins that take the perpetrator to a station between faith and disbelief (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn), where the person is called a transgressor (fasiq), and (b) minor sins that do not remove the person from faith. The author notes that the first to propose this intermediate station were Wasil ibn 'Ata' and 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. The passage ends with a promise to elaborate on the sayings of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila in a later purpose.

Key Terms
كفر
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That external acts of worship from other religions automatically make one a disbeliever.
Correction: The example of tying the sash shows that intent matters; without belief in the truth of the act, it is not kufr.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are children of believers considered believers?
A) Because they have explicit affirmation
B) Because of their parent's faith by legal ruling
C) Because they are born Muslims
D) Because they have not committed any sin

Key Takeaway
Kufr is defined as the opposite of iman, and external acts alone do not determine it without inner belief.

?

?

?
The passage says children of believers are considered believers by divine ruling. Are you living in a way that would make it a mercy for your children to be counted among the believers? What one change can you make in your faith practice to secure that for your family?

The Khawarij Position: Every Sin is Disbelief
Al-Jurjani presents the Khawarij view on sin and disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khawarij view that every sin is an act of disbelief and how this follows from their definition of iman as acts of obedience.

Core Idea
The Khawarij equate all sins with kufr because they define iman as complete obedience.

After establishing the principle that kufr is opposite to iman, Al-Jurjani turns to the Khawarij, who define iman as acts of obedience. Consequently, they hold that any sin, major or minor, is a form of disbelief. The author briefly notes that this view has been refuted in earlier discussions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Khawarij statement
Notice that the Khawarij say 'every disobedience is disbelief' (كل معصية كفر). This is a direct consequence of defining iman as all acts of obedience.
They make no distinction between major and minor sins.
2
See the link to the earlier principle
Recall the principle from the previous lesson: kufr is the opposite of iman. For the Khawarij, since iman is obedience, kufr is disobedience.
3
Understand the refutation
The author states that this view has been refuted (قد أبطلناه) without detailing the refutation here. Ask yourself why this position might be problematic.
The refutation likely involves that not all sins indicate rejection of God, and that believers can commit sins without losing faith.

Source Text

قوله : ( وبطلانه ظاهر لاستلزامه أن يكون النصارى مؤمنين .
قوله : ( فقالت :الخوارج كل معصية (كفر فإن قلت : يلزم السلف وأصحاب الأثر القائلين بأن الإيمان تصديق بالجنان وإقرار باللسان وعمل بالأركان أن يقولوا بما قال به الخوارج : بناء على أن الشيء ينتفي بانتفاء ركنه ، ولا منزلة عندهم بين الكفر والإيمان مع أنهم لا يجعلون تارك العمل خارجا من الإيمان ويقطعون بعدم خلوده في النار قلت : أجيب عنه بأن الإيمان يطلق على ما هو الأساس والأصل في دخول الجنة وهو التصديق وحده على ما هو الكامل المنجي، وهو الذي عد العمل ركناً منه وموضع الخلاف أن مطلق الاسم للأول أو الثاني، وقد أشرنا فيما سبق إلى وجه دفع آخر، فليتذكر.
بالإيمان لإيهامه عدم التصديق بل يحكم عليه بالفسق ( ويعبر عنهما ) أي عن المعاصي المخرجة إلى تلك المنزلة بالكبائر) كالقتل العمد والعدوان والزنا وشرب الخمر ونظائرهما وأول من أحدث القول بهذا الإخراج واصل بن عطاء وعمرو بن عبيد، ( ومنها ما لا يخرج أي قسم لا يخرج ) ككشف العورة والسفه، ويسمى بالصغائر ولا يوصف صاحبها بالكفر ولا بالفسق بل بالإيمان ) وسنزيده أي نزيد ما ذكرناه في هذا المقصد من قول الخوارج والمعتزلة بياناً في المقصد الذي يتلوه.
The third observation - the third purpose: on disbelief. Tying the sash not for veneration of the Christian religion and belief in its truth is not judged as his disbelief between him and God, as passed in prostration to the sun. It is not said: The children of believers have no affirmation, so it follows that they would be disbelievers not believers, and that is false; for we say: They are affirmers by legal ruling because it is known from necessity that God used to make the faith of one of the parents a faith for the children. (It) i.e. disbelief (according to each sect is opposite to what it explained faith with) just as with us it is opposite to what we explained it with. Whoever said: faith is knowledge of God, said disbelief is ignorance of God, and its falsehood is apparent. Whoever said: faith is acts of obedience, like the Khawarij and some Mu'tazila, said: disbelief is disobedience, but they differed. (The Khawarij said: every disobedience is disbelief, and we have refuted it. And the Mu'tazila said: acts of disobedience are) three divisions, since from them is what indicates ignorance of God and His oneness and what is possible for Him and what is not, and ignorance of His messenger's message like throwing the Quran into filth and uttering words indicating that, and reviling the messenger and disrespecting him, so it is disbelief. And from them is what does not indicate that, and it is two divisions: a division that takes its perpetrator to a station between the two stations i.e. between disbelief and faith, in the sense that he is not judged with disbelief because of the rest of his righteous deeds, and he is not judged with faith because it suggests lack of affirmation. Rather he is judged with transgression (fisq), and they are expressed as (major sins) like intentional murder and aggression and adultery and drinking wine and their likes. The first to originate the saying of this removal was Wasil ibn 'Ata' and 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. And from them is what does not remove i.e. a division that does not remove, like uncovering the private parts and foolishness, and it is called minor sins, and its possessor is not described with disbelief nor with transgression but with faith. And we will add i.e. increase what we mentioned in this purpose from the saying of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, clarification in the purpose that follows it.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification passage within the larger topic of disbelief (kufr). The author begins by presenting a scenario: tying the sash (a Christian practice) not for veneration or belief in its truth is not judged as disbelief between the person and God, referencing an earlier ruling on prostration to the sun. He then warns that children of believers cannot be denied faith, as they are considered affirmers legally because God made the faith of one parent count for the children. The main definition of kufr is given: each sect defines kufr as the opposite of what they define iman. For example, if iman is knowledge of God, kufr is ignorance of God. If iman is acts of obedience (as the Khawarij and some Mu'tazila hold), then kufr is disobedience (ma'siya). The author then explains the Mu'tazila division of sins into three categories: (1) sins that indicate ignorance of God and His messenger, which are kufr; (2) sins that do not indicate that, which are subdivided into (a) major sins that take the perpetrator to a station between faith and disbelief (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn), where the person is called a transgressor (fasiq), and (b) minor sins that do not remove the person from faith. The author notes that the first to propose this intermediate station were Wasil ibn 'Ata' and 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd. The passage ends with a promise to elaborate on the sayings of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila in a later purpose.

Key Terms
خوارج
معصية
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all sins are equal and remove a person from the faith entirely.
Correction: The Khawarij hold this view, but the author states it has been refuted; the prevailing Sunni view distinguishes between sins.

Checkpoint
What is the Khawarij definition of disbelief?
A) Ignorance of God
B) Every act of disobedience
C) Major sins only
D) Rejection of prophethood

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij assert that every sin constitutes disbelief, a position the author notes has been refuted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a sin, does your heart immediately question their faith? How does the Khawarij equation of every sin with disbelief challenge you to reflect on your own judgmental tendencies? What concrete step will you take today to replace that impulse with compassion?
?
If you define your own faith purely by your actions, how do you reconcile moments of disobedience with Allah's mercy? Are there traces of the Khawarij mindset in the way you evaluate your own spiritual state? Write down one sin you struggle with and consciously affirm that it does not nullify your iman.
?
The Khawarij view has been refuted, but its severity often lingers in how we treat others. Think of a person you have dismissed as 'less Muslim' due to their sins. Will you seek to understand the balanced Islamic position and change your heart toward them? Commit to one action today that reflects mercy over harshness.

What Is Kalam?

Mu'tazila: Three Categories of Sins
Al-Jurjani details the Mu'tazila classification of sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila classify sins into three categories: those that imply ignorance (kufr), major sins (leading to a station between faith and disbelief), and minor sins (not affecting faith).

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila distinguish between sins and only some constitute disbelief.

Unlike the Khawarij, the Mu'tazila do not equate all sins with disbelief. They divide sins into three distinct categories based on their implications. This lesson presents their detailed classification, including the famous concept of 'al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn' (the intermediate station) for major sins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The Mu'tazila say sins are of three types: (1) sins that indicate ignorance of God and His messenger (this is kufr), (2) sins that do not indicate ignorance but are major (these take the person to an intermediate station), and (3) sins that are minor (these do not affect faith).
Notice the examples given for each category.
2
Study the intermediate station
The second category includes major sins like murder and adultery. The person is not a kafir nor a believer but a fasiq (transgressor) in a station between faith and disbelief.
This concept was first proposed by Wasil ibn 'Ata' and 'Amr ibn 'Ubayd.
3
Understand the minor sins
Minor sins like uncovering private parts do not remove faith, so the person remains a believer.
The Mu'tazila thus avoid the Khawarij extreme while still maintaining that major sins have consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
